struct {\n\tobj      cty.Value\n\tobjPath  cty.Path\n\tattrPath cty.Path\n}\n\nvar _ argumentRetriever = attributeRetriever{}\n\nfunc newAttributeRetriever(obj cty.Value, attrPath cty.Path) attributeRetriever {\n\treturn attributeRetriever{\n\t\tobj:      obj,\n\t\tobjPath:  cty.Path{}, // Assumes that we're working relative to the root object\n\t\tattrPath: attrPath,\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (r attributeRetriever) Retrieve(diags *tfdiags.Diagnostics) (string, bool) {\n\tval, err := pathSafeApply(r.attrPath, r.obj)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\t*diags = diags.Append(attributeErrDiag(\n\t\t\t\"Invalid Path for Schema\",\n\t\t\t\"The S3 Backend unexpectedly provided a path that does not match the schema. \"+\n\t\t\t\t\"Please report this to the developers.\\n\\n\"+\n\t\t\t\t\"Path: \"+pathString(r.attrPath)+\"\\n\\n\"+\n\t\t\t\t\"Error: \"+err.Error(),\n\t\t\tr.objPath,\n\t\t))\n\t}\n\treturn stringValueOk(val)\n}\n\n// pathSafeApply applies a `cty.Path` to a `cty.Value`.\n// Unlike `path.Apply`, it does not return an error if it encounters a Null value\nfunc pathSafeApply(path cty.Path, obj cty.Value) (cty.Value, error) {\n\tif obj == cty.NilVal || obj.IsNull() {\n\t\treturn obj, nil\n\t}\n\tval := obj\n\tvar err error\n\tfor _, step := range path {\n\t\tval, err = step.Apply(val)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn cty.NilVal, err\n\t\t}\n\t\tif val == cty.NilVal || val.IsNull() {\n\t\t\treturn val, nil\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn val, nil\n}\n\ntype envvarRetriever struct {\n\tname string\n}\n\nvar _ argumentRetriever = envvarRetriever{}\n\nfunc newEnvvarRetriever(name string) envvarRetriever {\n\treturn envvarRetriever{\n\t\tname: name,\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (r envvarRetriever) Retrieve(_ *tfdiags.Diagnostics) (string, bool) {\n\tif v := os.Getenv(r.name); v != \"\" {\n\t\treturn v, true\n\t}\n\treturn \"\", false\n}\n\nfunc retrieveArgument(diags *tfdiags.Diagnostics, retrievers ...argumentRetriever) (string, bool) {\n\tfor _, retriever := range retrievers {\n\t\tif v, ok := retriever.Retrieve(diags); ok {\n\t\t\treturn v, true\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn \"\", false\n}\n\nfunc stringValue(val cty.Value) string {\n\tv, _ := stringValueOk(val)\n\treturn v\n}\n\nfunc stringValueOk(val cty.Value) (string, bool) {\n\tif val.IsNull() {\n\t\treturn \"\", false\n\t} else {\n\t\treturn val.AsString(), true\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc stringAttr(obj cty.Value, name string) string {\n\treturn stringValue(obj.GetAttr(name))\n}\n\nfunc stringAttrOk(obj cty.Value, name string) (string, bool) {\n\treturn diags\n}\n\n// Configure uses the provided configuration to set configuration fields\n// within the backend.\n//\n// The given configuration is assumed to have already been validated\n// against the schema returned by ConfigSchema and passed validation\n// via PrepareConfig.\nfunc (b *Backend) Configure(obj cty.Value) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n\tctx := context.TODO()\n\tlog := logger()\n\tlog = logWithOperation(log, operationBackendConfigure)\n\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\tif obj.IsNull() {\n\t\treturn diags\n\t}\n\n\tvar region string\n\tif v, ok := stringAttrOk(obj, \"region\"); ok {\n\t\tregion = v\n\t}\n\n\tif region != \"\" && !boolAttr(obj, \"skip_region_validation\") {\n\t\tif err := validation.SupportedRegion(region); err != nil {\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.AttributeValue(\n\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n\t\t\t\t\"Invalid region value\",\n\t\t\t\tfirstToUpper(err.Error()),\n\t\t\t\tcty.GetAttrPath(\"region\"),\n\t\t\t))\n\t\t\treturn struct {\n\tobj      cty.Value\n\tobjPath  cty.Path\n\tattrPath cty.Path\n}\n\nvar _ argumentRetriever = attributeRetriever{}\n\nfunc newAttributeRetriever(obj cty.Value, attrPath cty.Path) attributeRetriever {\n\treturn attributeRetriever{\n\t\tobj:      obj,\n\t\tobjPath:  cty.Path{}, // Assumes that we're working relative to the root object\n\t\tattrPath: attrPath,\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (r attributeRetriever) Retrieve(diags *tfdiags.Diagnostics) (string, bool) {\n\tval, err := pathSafeApply(r.attrPath, r.obj)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\t*diags = diags.Append(attributeErrDiag(\n\t\t\t\"Invalid Path for Schema\",\n\t\t\t\"The S3 Backend unexpectedly provided a path that does not match the schema. \"+\n\t\t\t\t\"Please report this to the developers.\\n\\n\"+\n\t\t\t\t\"Path: \"+pathString(r.attrPath)+\"\\n\\n\"+\n\t\t\t\t\"Error: \"+err.Error(),\n\t\t\tr.objPath,\n\t\t))\n\t}\n\treturn stringValueOk(val)\n}\n\n// pathSafeApply applies a `cty.Path` to a `cty.Value`.\n// Unlike `path.Apply`, it does not return an error if it encounters a Null value\nfunc pathSafeApply(path cty.Path, obj cty.Value) (cty.Value, error) {\n\tif obj == cty.NilVal || obj.IsNull() {\n\t\treturn obj, nil\n\t}\n\tval := obj\n\tvar err error\n\tfor _, step := range path {\n\t\tval, err = step.Apply(val)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn cty.NilVal, err\n\t\t}\n\t\tif val == cty.NilVal || val.IsNull() {\n\t\t\treturn val, nil\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn val, nil\n}\n\ntype envvarRetriever struct {\n\tname string\n}\n\nvar _ argumentRetriever = {\n\tv, _ := stringValueOk(val)\n\treturn v\n}\n\nfunc stringValueOk(val cty.Value) (string, bool) {\n\tif val.IsNull() {\n\t\treturn \"\", false\n\t} else {\n\t\treturn val.AsString(), true\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc stringAttr(obj cty.Value, name string) string {\n\treturn stringValue(obj.GetAttr(name))\n}\n\nfunc stringAttrOk(obj cty.Value, name string) (string, bool) {\n\treturn &list)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, false\n\t}\n\treturn list, true\n}\n\nfunc stringSetAttrOk(obj cty.Value, name string) ([]string, bool) {\n\treturn stringSetValueOk(obj.GetAttr(name))\n}\n\n// stringSetAttrDefaultEnvVarOk checks for a configured set of strings\n// in the provided argument name or environment variables. A configured\n// argument takes precedent over environment variables. An environment\n// variable is assumed to be as a single item, such as how the singular\n// AWS_SHARED_CONFIG_FILE variable aligns with the underlying\n// shared_config_files argument.\nfunc stringSetAttrDefaultEnvVarOk(obj cty.Value, name string, envvars ...string) ([]string, bool) {\n\tif v, ok := stringSetValueOk(obj.GetAttr(name)); !ok {\n\t\tfor _, envvar := range envvars {\n\t\t\tif v := os.Getenv(envvar); v != \"\" {\n\t\t\t\treturn []string{v}, true\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn nil, false\n\t} else {\n\t\treturn v, true\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc stringMapValueOk(val cty.Value) (map[string]string, bool) {\n\tvar m map[string]string\n\terr := gocty.FromCtyValue(val, &m)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, false\n\t}\n\treturn m, true\n}\n\nfunc stringMapAttrOk(obj cty.Value, name string) (map[string]string, bool) {\n\treturn stringMapValueOk(obj.GetAttr(name))\n}\n\nfunc boolAttr(obj cty.Value, name string) bool {\n\tv, _ := boolAttrOk(obj, name)\n\treturn v\n}\n\nfunc boolAttrOk(obj cty.Value, name string) (bool, bool) {\n\tif val := obj.GetAttr(name); val.IsNull() {\n\t\treturn false, false\n\t} else {\n\t\treturn val.True(), true\n\t}\n}\n\n// boolAttrDefaultEnvVarOk checks for a configured bool argument or a non-empty\n// value in any of the provided environment variables. If any of the environment\n// variables are non-empty, to boolean is considered true.\nfunc boolAttrDefaultEnvVarOk(obj cty.Value, name string, envvars ...string) (bool, bool) {\n\tif val := obj.GetAttr(name); val.IsNull() {\n\t\tfor _, envvar := range envvars {\n\t\t\tif v := os.Getenv(envvar); v != \"\" {\n\t\t\t\treturn true, true\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn false, false\n\t} else {\n\t\treturn val.True(), true\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc intAttr(obj cty.Value, name string) int {\n\tv, _ := intAttrOk(obj, name)\n\treturn v\n}\n\nfunc intAttrOk(obj cty.Value, name string) (int, bool) true\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc intAttrDefault(obj cty.Value, name string, def int) int {\n\tif v, ok := intAttrOk(obj, name); !ok {\n\t\treturn def\n\t} else {\n\t\treturn v\n\t}\n}\n\nconst encryptionKeyConflictEnvVarError = `Only one of \"kms_key_id\" and the environment variable \"AWS_SSE_CUSTOMER_KEY\" can be set.\n\nThe \"kms_key_id\" is used for encryption with KMS-Managed Keys (SSE-KMS)\nwhile \"AWS_SSE_CUSTOMER_KEY\" is used for encryption with customer-managed keys (SSE-C).\nPlease choose one or the other.`\n\nfunc validateNestedAttribute(objSchema schemaAttribute, obj cty.Value, objPath cty.Path, diags *tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tif obj.IsNull() {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tna, ok := objSchema.(singleNestedAttribute)\n\tif !ok {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tvalidator := objSchema.Validator()\n\tvalidator.ValidateAttr(obj, objPath, diags)\n\n\tfor name, attrSchema := range na.Attributes {\n\t\tattrPath := objPath.GetAttr(name)\n\t\tattrVal := obj.GetAttr(name)\n\n\t\tif attrVal.IsNull() {\n\t\t\tif attrSchema.SchemaAttribute().Required {\n\t\t\t\t*diags = diags.Append(requiredAttributeErrDiag(attrPath))\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif a, e := attrVal.Type(), attrSchema.SchemaAttribute().Type; a != e {\n\t\t\t*diags = {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01X1nPUS9nnGcMeZJQ126C3C","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01GpWMMcdH37KvKFeLWo5BdA","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0 Migration Guide\n\n## Overview\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 introduces several significant changes that require attention when upgrading from v1.9.0. The most impactful changes involve:\n\n1. **S3 Backend Configuration** - Removal of deprecated IAM role attributes and migration to `assume_role` block syntax\n2. **Moved Blocks Syntax** - New requirement to prepend `resource.` when referencing resources with type names matching reserved keywords\n3. **Sensitive Value Handling** - Improved mark propagation in conditional expressions that may result in more values being marked as sensitive\n4. **Ephemeral Resources and Values** - New feature introducing ephemeral input variables, outputs, and resources that don't persist to state files\n\nThis guide walks you through each breaking change with detailed migration instructions and examples.\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. S3 Backend: Removal of Deprecated IAM Role Attributes\n\n#### What Changed\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 removes deprecated IAM role assumption attributes from the S3 backend configuration. These attributes have been replaced with the `assume_role` block syntax. The deprecated attributes are:\n\n- `role_arn`\n- `session_name`\n- `external_id`\n- `assume_role_duration_seconds`\n- `assume_role_policy`\n- `assume_role_policy_arns`\n- `assume_role_tags`\n- `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys`\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nThe `assume_role` block provides a cleaner, more structured configuration format that aligns with AWS SDK standards and is easier to maintain. It also enables better validation and documentation.\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key    = \"terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # These attributes are deprecated\n    role_arn                   = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n    session_name               = \"terraform-session\"\n    external_id                = \"my-external-id\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds = 3600\n    assume_role_policy         = jsonencode({...})\n    assume_role_tags = {\n      Team = \"Infrastructure\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key    = \"terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # Use the assume_role block instead\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn    = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n      session_name = \"terraform-session\"\n      external_id = \"my-external-id\"\n\n      # Note: assume_role_duration_seconds becomes duration\n      duration = \"1h\"\n\n      # Policy restrictions\n      policy = jsonencode({...})\n\n      # Tags for the assume role session\n      tags = {\n        Team = \"Infrastructure\"\n      }\n\n      # Transitive tag keys\n      transitive_tag_keys = [\"Team\"]\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Assume Role Block Attribute Reference\n\nThe `assume_role` block supports the following attributes:\n\n| Attribute | Type | Required | Description |\n|-----------|------|----------|-------------|\n| `role_arn` | string | Yes | The ARN of the IAM role to assume |\n| `duration` | string | No | Session duration (15m to 12h). Valid units: ns, us, ms, s, h, m |\n| `session_name` | string | No | Name for the assume role session |\n| `external_id` | string | No | External ID for role assumption |\n| `policy` | string | No | IAM policy JSON to restrict permissions |\n| `policy_arns` | set of strings | No | ARNs of IAM policies for permission restrictions |\n| `source_identity` | string | No | Source identity specified by the principal |\n| `tags` | map of strings | No | Session tags |\n| `transitive_tag_keys` | set of strings | No | Tag keys to pass to subsequent sessions |\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Identify the deprecated attributes** in your S3 backend configuration\n2. **Convert the flat attributes to the assume_role block structure**:\n   - `role_arn` → `assume_role.role_arn`\n   - `session_name` → `assume_role.session_name`\n   - `external_id` → `assume_role.external_id`\n   - `assume_role_duration_seconds` → convert to duration string format (e.g., 3600 seconds = \"1h\")\n   - `assume_role_policy` → `assume_role.policy`\n   - `assume_role_policy_arns` → `assume_role.policy_arns`\n   - `assume_role_tags` → `assume_role.tags`\n   - `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` → `assume_role.transitive_tag_keys`\n3. **Test your configuration** with `terraform init` to ensure the migration is correct\n4. **No state migration needed** - this only affects backend configuration parsing\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **Duration format**: The new `duration` attribute expects a time duration string (e.g., \"1h\", \"30m\") instead of a number of seconds\n- **Validation stricter**: The `assume_role` block has stricter validation. Ensure your ARNs are valid and policies are valid JSON\n- **Empty attributes**: Remove any attributes you weren't actually using - they'll cause validation errors if present in the block\n- **Web identity**: If using OIDC/web identity, use `assume_role_with_web_identity` block instead, which has similar attributes\n\n---\n\n### 2. S3 Backend: New Native State Locking Support\n\n#### What Changed\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 introduces S3-native state locking via the new `use_lockfile` attribute. When enabled, Terraform uses S3's built-in locking mechanisms instead of (or in addition to) DynamoDB-based locking.\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nS3-native locking reduces dependencies on DynamoDB and provides better integration with S3's native capabilities. For users with existing DynamoDB locking, both locking mechanisms will be acquired to maintain compatibility.\n\n#### Configuration\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key    = \"terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # Enable S3-native locking (experimental)\n    use_lockfile = true\n\n    # DynamoDB locking can still be used alongside\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Behavior\n\n- When `use_lockfile = true`: Terraform uses S3-native locking\n- When using with DynamoDB: Both locking mechanisms are acquired for safety\n- When using S3-native only: Eliminates DynamoDB dependency\n- **Future deprecation notice**: DynamoDB-based locking will be deprecated in a future Terraform release\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Review your locking needs** - do you want to continue using DynamoDB or migrate to S3-native locking?\n2. **For S3-native only**:\n   ```hcl\n   terraform {\n     backend \"s3\" {\n       bucket       = \"my-terraform-state\"\n       key          = \"terraform.tfstate\"\n       region       = \"us-east-1\"\n       use_lockfile = true\n       # Remove or comment out dynamodb_table\n     }\n   }\n   ```\n3. **For gradual migration** (DynamoDB + S3-native):\n   ```hcl\n   terraform {\n     backend \"s3\" {\n       bucket         = \"my-terraform-state\"\n       key            = \"terraform.tfstate\"\n       region         = \"us-east-1\"\n       use_lockfile   = true\n       dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"  # Kept for compatibility\n     }\n   }\n   ```\n4. **Test with a non-production workspace first** to verify locking works as expected\n5. **Gradual rollout**: Update workspaces one at a time, monitoring for any lock-related issues\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **S3 permissions**: Ensure your IAM role has S3 permissions for the lock file operations (PutObject, GetObject, DeleteObject on the lock file)\n- **Race conditions**: If you have existing infrastructure using only DynamoDB locks, enable both temporarily to avoid lock conflicts during transition\n- **Lock file location**: S3-native locks are stored as hidden files in your S3 bucket. Ensure you don't have bucket policies that would interfere with lock file access\n\n---\n\n### 3. Moved Blocks: Reserved Keyword Prefix Requirement\n\n#### What Changed\n\nMoved blocks now strictly parse resource addresses and require that resource types matching reserved keywords be prefixed with `resource.`. This prevents ambiguity when a resource type name matches Terraform keywords.\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nReserved keywords like `count`, `module`, `var`, and `local` can be confused with actual resource types. By requiring explicit `resource.` prefixes, Terraform can unambiguously parse resource addresses in moved blocks.\n\n#### Reserved Keywords\n\nThe following keywords are now reserved and require the `resource.` prefix when used as resource type names in `moved` blocks:\n\n- `count`\n- `each`\n- `local`\n- `module`\n- `path`\n- `self`\n- `terraform`\n- `var`\n- `template`\n- `lazy`\n- `arg`\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\nIf you had a resource type matching a reserved keyword (less common but possible with custom providers):\n\n```hcl\n# This would work in v1.9.0 with custom providers that use these names\nmoved {\n  from = module.old_module[0]\n  to   = module.new_module[0]\n}\n\n# If a provider had a resource type called \"var\" (unusual but possible)\nmoved {\n  from = var.old\n  to   = var.new\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\nResources with type names matching reserved keywords must now be prefixed:\n\n```hcl\n# Module moves still work the same (module is a keyword)\nmoved {\n  from = module.old_module[0]\n  to   = module.new_module[0]\n}\n\n# But resource types matching keywords need resource. prefix\nmoved {\n  from = resource.var.old\n  to   = resource.var.new\n}\n\n# Similarly for custom provider resources with reserved keyword names\nmoved {\n  from = resource.count.old_name\n  to   = resource.count.new_name\n}\n```\n\n#### How to Migrate\n\n1. **Review existing moved blocks** in your configuration\n2. **Identify resource types that match reserved keywords** - these are rare\n3. **Add `resource.` prefix** to the resource portion of moved block addresses\n4. **Test the configuration** with `terraform validate`\n\n#### Examples\n\n```hcl\n# BEFORE (would fail in v1.10.0)\nmoved {\n  from = var.my_resource\n  to   = var.renamed_resource\n}\n\n# AFTER (works in v1.10.0)\nmoved {\n  from = resource.var.my_resource\n  to   = resource.var.renamed_resource\n}\n\n# Regular resource moves (unchanged)\nmoved {\n  from = aws_instance.example\n  to   = aws_instance.renamed\n}\n\n# The prefix is needed even for qualified resource moves\nmoved {\n  from = resource.module.foo.resource.count.example\n  to   = resource.module.foo.resource.count.renamed\n}\n```\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **Module moves are unaffected**: Module moves like `module.foo` don't need `resource.` prefix because `module` is always a module reference, not a resource type\n- **Data sources unaffected**: Data sources can still use the `data.` prefix or no prefix: `data.aws_ami.example` works without requiring `resource.data.`\n- **Custom provider resources**: If you use third-party providers with resource types matching keywords, you'll need to update your moved blocks\n- **Error messages**: If you get an error saying a keyword is reserved, check if you need to add the `resource.` prefix\n\n---\n\n### 4. Sensitive Value Handling: Improved Mark Propagation in Conditional Expressions\n\n#### What Changed\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 improves how sensitive marks are propagated through conditional expressions and for expressions. Previously, sensitive marks could be lost in certain combinations of conditional expressions and unknown values. Now, marks are combined from all values within the expression to ensure consistency.\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nThe previous behavior could hide sensitive information or cause inconsistencies where values were marked as sensitive during apply but not during plan. The new behavior ensures sensitive marks are preserved consistently, which is more secure and predictable.\n\n#### Impact\n\n- **More values marked sensitive**: Some values that previously lost their sensitive marks will now correctly be marked as sensitive\n- **Better security**: Sensitive information is now less likely to leak due to mark propagation issues\n- **Potential output changes**: State files and logs may show different sensitive redaction patterns\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\n```hcl\nlocals {\n  password = \"secret123\"\n  is_prod  = true\n}\n\noutput \"value\" {\n  value = local.is_prod ? sensitive(local.password) : \"default\"\n  # The output could lose the sensitive mark in certain cases\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\n```hcl\nlocals {\n  password = \"secret123\"\n  is_prod  = true\n}\n\noutput \"value\" {\n  value = local.is_prod ? sensitive(local.password) : \"default\"\n  # The output now correctly preserves the sensitive mark\n  # Output is always marked as sensitive due to mark propagation\n}\n```\n\n#### How Marks Are Combined\n\nIn v1.10.0, marks are combined as follows:\n\n1. **Conditional expressions**: If any branch of a conditional can produce a sensitive value, the result is marked sensitive\n2. **For expressions**: Sensitive marks are preserved through iteration\n3. **Object/list construction**: If any element is sensitive, the entire structure can be marked sensitive (depending on usage)\n\n#### Example: Conditional Expressions\n\n```hcl\n# All three branches can produce sensitive output, so result is marked sensitive\noutput \"secure_value\" {\n  value = var.use_secret ? var.secret :\n          var.use_default_secret ? sensitive(\"default-secret\") :\n          \"fallback\"\n  # Result is marked sensitive because branches 1 and 2 can produce sensitive values\n}\n\n# Mix of sensitive and non-sensitive branches\noutput \"mixed_value\" {\n  value = var.is_admin ? var.admin_key : var.user_key\n  # If var.admin_key is sensitive, output is marked sensitive\n}\n```\n\n#### Using `nonsensitive()` to Override\n\nIf you have legitimate reasons to remove sensitive marks, use the `nonsensitive()` function:\n\n```hcl\noutput \"declassified_value\" {\n  value = nonsensitive(var.secret_that_should_be_visible)\n  # Explicitly removes the sensitive mark\n  # Be cautious: this value will appear in plain text in logs and state\n}\n\noutput \"conditional_declassified\" {\n  value = var.show_secret ? nonsensitive(var.secret) : \"hidden\"\n  # Only declassified when condition is true\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Test your configuration** with `terraform plan` in v1.10.0\n2. **Review output changes** - note which values are now marked as sensitive\n3. **Evaluate if the behavior is correct** for your use case\n4. **Use `nonsensitive()`** only if you have legitimate reasons to declassify values\n5. **Update tests and validations** if you have checks that verify sensitive status\n\n#### Common Issues and Solutions\n\n**Issue**: Outputs that worked in v1.9.0 now show as sensitive in v1.10.0\n\n```hcl\n# v1.9.0 - might not mark as sensitive\noutput \"value\" {\n  value = var.condition ? sensitive(local.secret) : \"default\"\n}\n\n# v1.10.0 - marked as sensitive due to conditional branch\n# Solution 1: Accept the more secure behavior\n# Solution 2: Use nonsensitive() if truly not a secret\noutput \"value\" {\n  value = nonsensitive(\n    var.condition ? sensitive(local.secret) : \"default\"\n  )\n}\n```\n\n**Issue**: Plan shows sensitive values but apply shows them in plain text\n\n```hcl\n# This indicates inconsistent mark propagation in v1.9.0\n# In v1.10.0, it will be consistent\n# Solution: Ensure all code paths that handle secrets explicitly mark them\n\noutput \"config_value\" {\n  # GOOD: Consistent marking\n  value = var.is_secret ? sensitive(data.external.config.result.value) : \"default\"\n\n  # AVOID: Inconsistent marking\n  value = var.is_secret ? data.external.config.result.value : \"default\"\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## New Features with Migration Impact\n\n### Ephemeral Resources and Values\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 introduces ephemeral resources and values - data that exists only in memory during a single phase and cannot be persisted to state files or plan files.\n\n#### What Are Ephemeral Values?\n\nEphemeral values are:\n- Only available during Terraform evaluation\n- Not persisted to state files\n- Not persisted to saved plan files\n- Useful for handling secrets that should never be stored\n- Automatically lost between phases\n\n#### Ephemeral Input Variables\n\nYou can now mark input variables as ephemeral:\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"api_key\" {\n  type        = string\n  sensitive   = true\n  ephemeral   = true\n  description = \"API key that should not be stored in state\"\n}\n\nresource \"example_api\" \"example\" {\n  api_key = var.api_key\n  # api_key is passed to the provider but not stored in state\n}\n```\n\n**Key points**:\n- Ephemeral variables must be provided via command-line, environment variables, or other non-state sources\n- They're not stored in state files\n- Modules cannot accept ephemeral variables yet (planned for future release)\n- Combining `ephemeral = true` and `default` is allowed, but the default won't be used for ephemeral variables\n\n#### Ephemeral Outputs\n\nYou can mark outputs as ephemeral:\n\n```hcl\noutput \"temporary_token\" {\n  ephemeral   = true\n  description = \"A token that expires quickly and shouldn't be persisted\"\n  value       = aws_cognito_user_pool_client.app.client_secret\n}\n\n# Usage: terraform output temporary_token\n# The value is returned but NOT saved to state\n```\n\n**Key points**:\n- Ephemeral outputs are displayed at the end of apply/plan but not saved\n- They're useful for temporary credentials or one-time use values\n- Can be referenced in the same module but not persisted between runs\n\n#### Ephemeral Resources\n\nNew `ephemeral` resource blocks read data anew each time Terraform runs:\n\n```hcl\n# Define a custom provider that supports ephemeral resources\nephemeral \"custom_provider_ephemeral_data\" \"dynamic_config\" {\n  # Config that's fetched fresh each run\n  endpoint = var.endpoint\n  # This data is never stored in state\n}\n\nresource \"example_resource\" \"main\" {\n  # Can use data from ephemeral resource\n  config = ephemeral.custom_provider_ephemeral_data.dynamic_config.result\n\n  # The config is used but ephemeral values aren't persisted\n  lifecycle {\n    ignore_changes = [config]  # Often needed for ephemeral data\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**Key points**:\n- Only custom providers that support ephemeral resources can use this feature\n- Ephemeral resources are evaluated fresh in each phase\n- They don't persist to state\n- References to ephemeral resources can only be used in certain contexts\n\n#### The `ephemeralasnull` Function\n\nUse this function to convert ephemeral values to non-ephemeral null values:\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"secret\" {\n  type        = string\n  ephemeral   = true\n  sensitive   = true\n}\n\noutput \"safe_value\" {\n  value = ephemeralasnull(var.secret)\n  # If var.secret is ephemeral, returns null\n  # If var.secret is provided, passes through as-is\n  # Useful for optional ephemeral values\n}\n\noutput \"with_fallback\" {\n  value = ephemeralasnull(var.secret) != null ? var.secret : \"default\"\n  # Use ephemeral value if available, otherwise use default\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Impact and Planning\n\n**If you're upgrading to v1.10.0**:\n\n1. **No immediate action needed** if you don't use ephemeral features\n2. **Review sensitive variables** - consider if any should be ephemeral instead\n3. **Evaluate secret handling** - ephemeral values provide better secret security\n4. **Plan for provider support** - ephemeral resources require provider support\n\n**Best practices for secrets**:\n\n```hcl\n# BEFORE (v1.9.0) - Secret stored in state\nvariable \"api_key\" {\n  type        = string\n  sensitive   = true\n  # Value stored in state, just marked sensitive\n}\n\n# AFTER (v1.10.0) - Ephemeral secret\nvariable \"api_key\" {\n  type        = string\n  sensitive   = true\n  ephemeral   = true\n  # Value NOT stored in state, truly temporary\n}\n\nresource \"api_client\" \"main\" {\n  api_key = var.api_key\n}\n```\n\n#### Limitations and Future Roadmap\n\nCurrent limitations (as of v1.10.0):\n\n- **Module inputs**: Ephemeral variables cannot be passed to module inputs (planned for future)\n- **State references**: Ephemeral values cannot reference state\n- **Limited provider support**: Only some providers support ephemeral resources\n- **Cross-run limitations**: Ephemeral values are lost between plan and apply\n\nFuture improvements:\n- Ephemeral module variables\n- Broader provider support for ephemeral resources\n- Additional ephemeral value utilities\n\n---\n\n## Testing Your Migration\n\n### Pre-Upgrade Testing\n\nBefore upgrading to v1.10.0, validate your configuration in v1.9.0:\n\n```bash\n# Run full validation and tests\nterraform validate\nterraform plan -out=tfplan.out\n```\n\n### Post-Upgrade Testing\n\nAfter upgrading, perform these tests:\n\n1. **Configuration Validation**\n   ```bash\n   terraform validate\n   ```\n   Look for errors about:\n   - Deprecated S3 backend attributes (migrate to assume_role block)\n   - Moved block syntax issues (add resource. prefix if needed)\n   - New ephemeral-related errors\n\n2. **State Compatibility**\n   ```bash\n   # Plan against existing state\n   terraform plan\n   ```\n   Should show no unexpected changes. If you see changes:\n   - Review sensitive mark propagation (may be more values marked now)\n   - Check ephemeral variable usage\n   - Verify S3 backend configuration\n\n3. **S3 Backend Testing**\n   ```bash\n   # Reinitialize to test new backend configuration\n   terraform init -reconfigure\n\n   # Verify locking works (if enabled)\n   # Try concurrent operations or observe lock behavior\n   ```\n\n4. **Sensitive Value Testing**\n   ```bash\n   # Check plan output for sensitive redaction\n   terraform plan\n\n   # Look for sensitive values being correctly redacted\n   # If too many values are redacted, use nonsensitive() if appropriate\n   ```\n\n### Rollback Testing\n\nTest your rollback procedure:\n\n1. **Keep v1.9.0 and v1.10.0 binaries**:\n   ```bash\n   # Test that you can switch back to v1.9.0\n   terraform version  # Should show v1.10.0\n\n   # Switch to v1.9.0\n   # Rerun plan - should work without breaking changes\n   ```\n\n2. **State file compatibility**:\n   - State files from v1.10.0 can be read by v1.9.0\n   - No state migration is needed\n   - Rolling back to v1.9.0 doesn't require special steps\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\nIf you encounter issues after upgrading to v1.10.0, you can safely rollback to v1.9.0:\n\n### Rollback Procedure\n\n1. **Switch back to Terraform v1.9.0**:\n   ```bash\n   # Using tfenv\n   tfenv install 1.9.0\n   tfenv use 1.9.0\n\n   # Or using direct binary\n   export PATH=\"/path/to/terraform-1.9.0:$PATH\"\n\n   # Verify\n   terraform version\n   ```\n\n2. **Revert configuration changes** (if you made them):\n   - Revert S3 backend to old attribute format if you changed it\n   - Revert moved block prefixes if you added resource.\n   - Continue using v1.9.0 code\n\n3. **No state file migration needed**:\n   ```bash\n   # State files are fully compatible between versions\n   terraform plan  # Should work immediately\n   ```\n\n4. **Identify the issue** that required rollback:\n   - Check if it's related to your custom configuration\n   - Review error messages for hints\n   - Search Terraform issues: https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues\n\n### Common Rollback Scenarios\n\n**Scenario: S3 backend assume_role block not working**\n```bash\n# Rollback and use the old deprecated attributes temporarily\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket     = \"my-bucket\"\n    key        = \"state\"\n    region     = \"us-east-1\"\n    role_arn   = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"  # Use old format\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**Scenario: Sensitive mark propagation breaking output validation**\n```bash\n# Rollback to v1.9.0\nterraform version\n# Check if the issue was specific to v1.10.0 behavior\n# If so, report the issue: https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/new\n```\n\n**Scenario: Ephemeral variables causing issues**\n```bash\n# Remove ephemeral = true from variables and outputs\n# Switch back to regular sensitive = true\nterraform {\n  # Clear any ephemeral configuration\n}\n```\n\n### When to Stay on v1.9.0\n\nConsider staying on v1.9.0 if:\n\n- You have critical workloads that cannot tolerate mark propagation changes\n- Your providers don't support ephemeral resources (not needed yet)\n- You need more time to update S3 backend configuration\n- You're waiting for certain ephemeral features (like module variables)\n\n### Migration Strategy\n\nFor safer upgrades:\n\n1. **Stage the upgrade**:\n   - Upgrade non-production workspaces first\n   - Test for 1-2 weeks\n   - Gradually upgrade production workspaces\n\n2. **Run both versions in parallel**:\n   - Keep v1.9.0 in one workspace\n   - Use v1.10.0 in another\n   - Compare results and behavior\n\n3. **Automated testing**:\n   - Add tests for sensitive mark behavior\n   - Test conditional expressions with sensitive values\n   - Validate S3 backend configuration\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Changes\n\n| Change | Impact | Action Required |\n|--------|--------|-----------------|\n| S3 backend deprecated attributes | Breaking | Migrate to `assume_role` block |\n| S3 backend new locking | Optional | Add `use_lockfile = true` if desired |\n| Moved block keyword prefixes | Breaking (rare) | Add `resource.` prefix if using reserved keywords |\n| Sensitive mark propagation | Behavioral | Review output redaction; use `nonsensitive()` if needed |\n| Ephemeral resources | New feature | Adopt for secret handling if desired |\n| Ephemeral variables | New feature | Mark sensitive variables as ephemeral |\n| Ephemeral outputs | New feature | Mark temporary outputs as ephemeral |\n\n---\n\n## Additional Resources\n\n- **Terraform v1.10.0 Release Notes**: https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/releases/tag/v1.10.0\n- **Terraform S3 Backend Documentation**: https://www.terraform.io/language/settings/backends/s3\n- **Terraform Moved Block Documentation**: https://www.terraform.io/language/state/moved\n- **Terraform Sensitive Values**: https://www.terraform.io/language/functions/sensitive\n- **Issue Tracker**: https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues\n\n---\n\n## Getting Help\n\nIf you encounter migration issues:\n\n1. **Check the error message** - The exact error message\n   - Steps to reproduce\n   - Your version information (`terraform version`)\n\n4. **Community resources**:\n   - Terraform Discuss: https://discuss.hashicorp.com/c/terraform-core/\n   - The most impactful changes involve:\n\n1. **S3 Backend Configuration** - Removal of deprecated IAM role attributes and migration to `assume_role` block syntax\n2. **Moved Blocks Syntax** - New requirement to prepend `resource.` when referencing resources with type names matching reserved keywords\n3. **Sensitive Value Handling** - Improved mark propagation in conditional expressions that may result in more values being marked as sensitive\n4. **Ephemeral Resources and Values** - New feature introducing ephemeral input variables, outputs, and resources that don't persist to state files\n\nThis guide walks you through each breaking change with detailed migration instructions and examples.\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. S3 Backend: Removal of Deprecated IAM Role Attributes\n\n#### What Changed\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 removes deprecated IAM role assumption attributes from the S3 backend configuration. These attributes have been replaced with the `assume_role` block syntax. The deprecated attributes are:\n\n- `role_arn`\n- `session_name`\n- `external_id`\n- `assume_role_duration_seconds`\n- `assume_role_policy`\n- `assume_role_policy_arns`\n- `assume_role_tags`\n- `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys`\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nThe `assume_role` block provides a cleaner, more structured configuration format that aligns with AWS SDK standards and is easier to maintain. It also enables better validation and documentation.\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key    = \"terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # These attributes are deprecated\n    role_arn                   = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n    session_name               = \"terraform-session\"\n    external_id                = \"my-external-id\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds = 3600\n    assume_role_policy         = jsonencode({...})\n    assume_role_tags = {\n      Team = \"Infrastructure\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key    = \"terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # Use the assume_role block instead\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn    = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n      session_name = \"terraform-session\"\n      external_id = \"my-external-id\"\n\n      # Note: assume_role_duration_seconds becomes duration\n      duration = \"1h\"\n\n      # Policy restrictions\n      policy = jsonencode({...})\n\n      # Tags for the assume role session\n      tags = {\n        Team = \"Infrastructure\"\n      }\n\n      # Transitive tag keys\n      transitive_tag_keys = [\"Team\"]\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Assume Role Block Attribute Reference\n\nThe `assume_role` block supports the following attributes:\n\n| Attribute | Type | Required | Description |\n|-----------|------|----------|-------------|\n| `role_arn` | string | Yes | The ARN of the IAM role to assume |\n| `duration` | string | No | Session duration (15m to 12h). Valid units: ns, us, ms, s, h, m |\n| `session_name` | string | No | Name for the assume role session |\n| `external_id` | string | No | External ID for role assumption |\n| `policy` | string | No | IAM policy JSON to restrict permissions |\n| `policy_arns` | set of strings | No | ARNs of IAM policies for permission restrictions |\n| `source_identity` | string | No | Source identity specified by the principal |\n| `tags` | map of strings | No | Session tags |\n| `transitive_tag_keys` | set of strings | No | Tag keys to pass to subsequent sessions |\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Identify the deprecated attributes** in your S3 backend configuration\n2. **Convert the flat attributes to the assume_role block structure**:\n   - `role_arn` → `assume_role.role_arn`\n   - `session_name` → `assume_role.session_name`\n   - `external_id` → `assume_role.external_id`\n   - `assume_role_duration_seconds` → convert to duration string format (e.g., 3600 seconds = \"1h\")\n   - `assume_role_policy` → `assume_role.policy`\n   - `assume_role_policy_arns` → `assume_role.policy_arns`\n   - `assume_role_tags` → `assume_role.tags`\n   - `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` → `assume_role.transitive_tag_keys`\n3. **Test your configuration** with `terraform init` to ensure the migration is correct\n4. **No state migration needed** - this only affects backend configuration parsing\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **Duration format**: The new `duration` attribute expects a time duration string (e.g., \"1h\", \"30m\") instead of a number of seconds\n- **Validation stricter**: The `assume_role` block has stricter validation. Ensure your ARNs are valid and policies are valid JSON\n- **Empty attributes**: Remove any attributes you weren't actually using - they'll cause validation errors if present in the block\n- **Web identity**: If using OIDC/web identity, use `assume_role_with_web_identity` block instead, which has similar attributes\n\n---\n\n### 2. S3 Backend: New Native State Locking Support\n\n#### What Changed\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 introduces S3-native state locking via the new `use_lockfile` attribute. When enabled, Terraform uses S3's built-in locking mechanisms instead of (or in addition to) DynamoDB-based locking.\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nS3-native locking reduces dependencies on DynamoDB and provides better integration with S3's native capabilities. For users with existing DynamoDB locking, both locking mechanisms will be acquired to maintain compatibility.\n\n#### Configuration\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key    = \"terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # Enable S3-native locking (experimental)\n    use_lockfile = true\n\n    # DynamoDB locking can still be used alongside\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Behavior\n\n- When `use_lockfile = true`: Terraform uses S3-native locking\n- When using with DynamoDB: Both locking mechanisms are acquired for safety\n- When using S3-native only: Eliminates DynamoDB dependency\n- **Future deprecation notice**: DynamoDB-based locking will be deprecated in a future Terraform release\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Review your locking needs** - do you want to continue using DynamoDB or migrate to S3-native locking?\n2. **For S3-native only**:\n   ```hcl\n   terraform {\n     backend \"s3\" {\n       bucket       = \"my-terraform-state\"\n       key          = \"terraform.tfstate\"\n       region       = \"us-east-1\"\n       use_lockfile = true\n       # Remove or comment out dynamodb_table\n     }\n   }\n   ```\n3. **For gradual migration** (DynamoDB + S3-native):\n   ```hcl\n   terraform {\n     backend \"s3\" {\n       bucket         = \"my-terraform-state\"\n       key            = \"terraform.tfstate\"\n       region         = \"us-east-1\"\n       use_lockfile   = true\n       dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"  # Kept for compatibility\n     }\n   }\n   ```\n4. **Test with a non-production workspace first** to verify locking works as expected\n5. **Gradual rollout**: Update workspaces one at a time, monitoring for any lock-related issues\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **S3 permissions**: Ensure your IAM role has S3 permissions for the lock file operations (PutObject, GetObject, DeleteObject on the lock file)\n- **Race conditions**: If you have existing infrastructure using only DynamoDB locks, enable both temporarily to avoid lock conflicts during transition\n- **Lock file location**: S3-native locks are stored as hidden files in your S3 bucket. Ensure you don't have bucket policies that would interfere with lock file access\n\n---\n\n### 3. Moved Blocks: Reserved Keyword Prefix Requirement\n\n#### What Changed\n\nMoved blocks now strictly parse resource addresses and require that resource types matching reserved keywords be prefixed with `resource.`. This prevents ambiguity when a resource type name matches Terraform keywords.\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nReserved keywords like `count`, `module`, `var`, and `local` can be confused with actual resource types. By requiring explicit `resource.` prefixes, Terraform can unambiguously parse resource addresses in moved blocks.\n\n#### Reserved Keywords\n\nThe following keywords are now reserved and require the `resource.` prefix when used as resource type names in `moved` blocks:\n\n- `count`\n- `each`\n- `local`\n- `module`\n- `path`\n- `self`\n- `terraform`\n- `var`\n- `template`\n- `lazy`\n- `arg`\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\nIf you had a resource type matching a reserved keyword (less common but possible with custom providers):\n\n```hcl\n# This would work in v1.9.0 with custom providers that use these names\nmoved {\n  from = module.old_module[0]\n  to   = module.new_module[0]\n}\n\n# If a provider had a resource type called \"var\" (unusual but possible)\nmoved {\n  from = var.old\n  to   = var.new\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\nResources with type names matching reserved keywords must now be prefixed:\n\n```hcl\n# Module moves still work the same (module is a keyword)\nmoved {\n  from = module.old_module[0]\n  to   = module.new_module[0]\n}\n\n# But resource types matching keywords need resource. prefix\nmoved {\n  from = resource.var.old\n  to   = resource.var.new\n}\n\n# Similarly for custom provider resources with reserved keyword names\nmoved {\n  from = resource.count.old_name\n  to   = resource.count.new_name\n}\n```\n\n#### How to Migrate\n\n1. **Review existing moved blocks** in your configuration\n2. **Identify resource types that match reserved keywords** - these are rare\n3. **Add `resource.` prefix** to the resource portion of moved block addresses\n4. **Test the configuration** with `terraform validate`\n\n#### Examples\n\n```hcl\n# BEFORE (would fail in v1.10.0)\nmoved {\n  from = var.my_resource\n  to   = var.renamed_resource\n}\n\n# AFTER (works in v1.10.0)\nmoved {\n  from = resource.var.my_resource\n  to   = resource.var.renamed_resource\n}\n\n# Regular resource moves (unchanged)\nmoved {\n  from = aws_instance.example\n  to   = aws_instance.renamed\n}\n\n# The prefix is needed even for qualified resource moves\nmoved {\n  from = resource.module.foo.resource.count.example\n  to   = resource.module.foo.resource.count.renamed\n}\n```\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **Module moves are unaffected**: Module moves like `module.foo` don't need `resource.` prefix because `module` is always a module reference, not a resource type\n- **Data sources unaffected**: Data sources can still use the `data.` prefix or no prefix: `data.aws_ami.example` works without requiring `resource.data.`\n- **Custom provider resources**: If you use third-party providers with resource types matching keywords, you'll need to update your moved blocks\n- **Error messages**: If you get an error saying a keyword is reserved, check if you need to add the `resource.` prefix\n\n---\n\n### 4. Sensitive Value Handling: Improved Mark Propagation in Conditional Expressions\n\n#### What Changed\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 improves how sensitive marks are propagated through conditional expressions and for expressions. Previously, sensitive marks could be lost in certain combinations of conditional expressions and unknown values. Now, marks are combined from all values within the expression to ensure consistency.\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nThe previous behavior could hide sensitive information or cause inconsistencies where values were marked as sensitive during apply but not during plan. The new behavior ensures sensitive marks are preserved consistently, which is more secure and predictable.\n\n#### Impact\n\n- **More values marked sensitive**: Some values that previously lost their sensitive marks will now correctly be marked as sensitive\n- **Better security**: Sensitive information is now less likely to leak due to mark propagation issues\n- **Potential output changes**: State files and logs may show different sensitive redaction patterns\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\n```hcl\nlocals {\n  password = \"secret123\"\n  is_prod  = true\n}\n\noutput \"value\" {\n  value = local.is_prod ? sensitive(local.password) : \"default\"\n  # The output could lose the sensitive mark in certain cases\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\n```hcl\nlocals {\n  password = \"secret123\"\n  is_prod  = true\n}\n\noutput \"value\" {\n  value = local.is_prod ? sensitive(local.password) : \"default\"\n  # The output now correctly preserves the sensitive mark\n  # Output is always marked as sensitive due to mark propagation\n}\n```\n\n#### How Marks Are Combined\n\nIn v1.10.0, marks are combined as follows:\n\n1. **Conditional expressions**: If any branch of a conditional can produce a sensitive value, the result is marked sensitive\n2. **For expressions**: Sensitive marks are preserved through iteration\n3. **Object/list construction**: If any element is sensitive, the entire structure can be marked sensitive (depending on usage)\n\n#### Example: Conditional Expressions\n\n```hcl\n# All three branches can produce sensitive output, so result is marked sensitive\noutput \"secure_value\" {\n  value = var.use_secret ? var.secret :\n          var.use_default_secret ? sensitive(\"default-secret\") :\n          \"fallback\"\n  # Result is marked sensitive because branches 1 and 2 can produce sensitive values\n}\n\n# Mix of sensitive and non-sensitive branches\noutput \"mixed_value\" {\n  value = var.is_admin ? var.admin_key : var.user_key\n  # If var.admin_key is sensitive, output is marked sensitive\n}\n```\n\n#### Using `nonsensitive()` to Override\n\nIf you have legitimate reasons to remove sensitive marks, use the `nonsensitive()` function:\n\n```hcl\noutput \"declassified_value\" {\n  value = nonsensitive(var.secret_that_should_be_visible)\n  # Explicitly removes the sensitive mark\n  # Be cautious: this value will appear in plain text in logs and state\n}\n\noutput \"conditional_declassified\" {\n  value = var.show_secret ? nonsensitive(var.secret) : \"hidden\"\n  # Only declassified when condition is true\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Test your configuration** with `terraform plan` in v1.10.0\n2. **Review output changes** - note which values are now marked as sensitive\n3. **Evaluate if the behavior is correct** for your use case\n4. **Use `nonsensitive()`** only if you have legitimate reasons to declassify values\n5. **Update tests and validations** if you have checks that verify sensitive status\n\n#### Common Issues and Solutions\n\n**Issue**: Outputs that worked in v1.9.0 now show as sensitive in v1.10.0\n\n```hcl\n# v1.9.0 - might not mark as sensitive\noutput \"value\" {\n  value = var.condition ? sensitive(local.secret) : \"default\"\n}\n\n# v1.10.0 - marked as sensitive due to conditional branch\n# Solution 1: Accept the more secure behavior\n# Solution 2: Use nonsensitive() if truly not a secret\noutput \"value\" {\n  value = nonsensitive(\n    var.condition ? sensitive(local.secret) : \"default\"\n  )\n}\n```\n\n**Issue**: Plan shows sensitive values but apply shows them in plain text\n\n```hcl\n# This indicates inconsistent mark propagation in v1.9.0\n# In v1.10.0, it will be consistent\n# Solution: Ensure all code paths that handle secrets explicitly mark them\n\noutput \"config_value\" {\n  # GOOD: Consistent marking\n  value = var.is_secret ? sensitive(data.external.config.result.value) : \"default\"\n\n  # AVOID: Inconsistent marking\n  value = var.is_secret ? data.external.config.result.value : \"default\"\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## New Features with Migration Impact\n\n### Ephemeral Resources and Values\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 introduces ephemeral resources and values - data that exists only in memory during a single phase and cannot be persisted to state files or plan files.\n\n#### What Are Ephemeral Values?\n\nEphemeral values are:\n- Only available during Terraform evaluation\n- Not persisted to state files\n- Not persisted to saved plan files\n- Useful for handling secrets that should never be stored\n- Automatically lost between phases\n\n#### Ephemeral Input Variables\n\nYou can now mark input variables as ephemeral:\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"api_key\" {\n  type        = string\n  sensitive   = true\n  ephemeral   = true\n  description = \"API key that should not be stored in state\"\n}\n\nresource \"example_api\" \"example\" {\n  api_key = var.api_key\n  # api_key is passed to the provider but not stored in state\n}\n```\n\n**Key points**:\n- Ephemeral variables must be provided via command-line, environment variables, or other non-state sources\n- They're not stored in state files\n- Modules cannot accept ephemeral variables yet (planned for future release)\n- Combining `ephemeral = true` and `default` is allowed, but the default won't be used for ephemeral variables\n\n#### Ephemeral Outputs\n\nYou can mark outputs as ephemeral:\n\n```hcl\noutput \"temporary_token\" {\n  ephemeral   = true\n  description = \"A token that expires quickly and shouldn't be persisted\"\n  value       = aws_cognito_user_pool_client.app.client_secret\n}\n\n# Usage: terraform output temporary_token\n# The value is returned but NOT saved to state\n```\n\n**Key points**:\n- Ephemeral outputs are displayed at the end of apply/plan but not saved\n- They're useful for temporary credentials or one-time use values\n- Can be referenced in the same module but not persisted between runs\n\n#### Ephemeral Resources\n\nNew `ephemeral` resource blocks read data anew each time Terraform runs:\n\n```hcl\n# Define a custom provider that supports ephemeral resources\nephemeral \"custom_provider_ephemeral_data\" \"dynamic_config\" {\n  # Config that's fetched fresh each run\n  endpoint = var.endpoint\n  # This data is never stored in state\n}\n\nresource \"example_resource\" \"main\" {\n  # Can use data from ephemeral resource\n  config = ephemeral.custom_provider_ephemeral_data.dynamic_config.result\n\n  # The config is used but ephemeral values aren't persisted\n  lifecycle {\n    ignore_changes = [config]  # Often needed for ephemeral data\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**Key points**:\n- Only custom providers that support ephemeral resources can use this feature\n- Ephemeral resources are evaluated fresh in each phase\n- They don't persist to state\n- References to ephemeral resources can only be used in certain contexts\n\n#### The `ephemeralasnull` Function\n\nUse this function to convert ephemeral values to non-ephemeral null values:\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"secret\" {\n  type        = string\n  ephemeral   = true\n  sensitive   = true\n}\n\noutput \"safe_value\" {\n  value = ephemeralasnull(var.secret)\n  # If var.secret is ephemeral, returns null\n  # If var.secret is provided, passes through as-is\n  # Useful for optional ephemeral values\n}\n\noutput \"with_fallback\" {\n  value = ephemeralasnull(var.secret) != null ? var.secret : \"default\"\n  # Use ephemeral value if available, otherwise use default\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Impact and Planning\n\n**If you're upgrading to v1.10.0**:\n\n1. **No immediate action needed** if you don't use ephemeral features\n2. **Review sensitive variables** - consider if any should be ephemeral instead\n3. **Evaluate secret handling** - ephemeral values provide better secret security\n4. **Plan for provider support** - ephemeral resources require provider support\n\n**Best practices for secrets**:\n\n```hcl\n# BEFORE (v1.9.0) - Secret stored in state\nvariable \"api_key\" {\n  type        = string\n  sensitive   = true\n  # Value stored in state, just marked sensitive\n}\n\n# AFTER (v1.10.0) - Ephemeral secret\nvariable \"api_key\" {\n  type        = string\n  sensitive   = true\n  ephemeral   = true\n  # Value NOT stored in state, truly temporary\n}\n\nresource \"api_client\" \"main\" {\n  api_key = var.api_key\n}\n```\n\n#### Limitations and Future Roadmap\n\nCurrent limitations (as of v1.10.0):\n\n- **Module inputs**: Ephemeral variables cannot be passed to module inputs (planned for future)\n- **State references**: Ephemeral values cannot reference state\n- **Limited provider support**: Only some providers support ephemeral resources\n- **Cross-run limitations**: Ephemeral values are lost between plan and apply\n\nFuture improvements:\n- Ephemeral module variables\n- Broader provider support for ephemeral resources\n- Additional ephemeral value utilities\n\n---\n\n## Testing Your Migration\n\n### Pre-Upgrade Testing\n\nBefore upgrading to v1.10.0, validate your configuration in v1.9.0:\n\n```bash\n# Run full validation and tests\nterraform validate\nterraform plan -out=tfplan.out\n```\n\n### Post-Upgrade Testing\n\nAfter upgrading, perform these tests:\n\n1. **Configuration Validation**\n   ```bash\n   terraform validate\n   ```\n   Look for errors about:\n   - Deprecated S3 backend attributes (migrate to assume_role block)\n   - Moved block syntax issues (add resource. prefix if needed)\n   - New ephemeral-related errors\n\n2. **State Compatibility**\n   ```bash\n   # Plan against existing state\n   terraform plan\n   ```\n   Should show no unexpected changes. If you see changes:\n   - Review sensitive mark propagation (may be more values marked now)\n   - Check ephemeral variable usage\n   - Verify S3 backend configuration\n\n3. **S3 Backend Testing**\n   ```bash\n   # Reinitialize to test new backend configuration\n   terraform init -reconfigure\n\n   # Verify locking works (if enabled)\n   # Try concurrent operations or observe lock behavior\n   ```\n\n4. **Sensitive Value Testing**\n   ```bash\n   # Check plan output for sensitive redaction\n   terraform plan\n\n   # Look for sensitive values being correctly redacted\n   # If too many values are redacted, use nonsensitive() if appropriate\n   ```\n\n### Rollback Testing\n\nTest your rollback procedure:\n\n1. **Keep v1.9.0 and v1.10.0 binaries**:\n   ```bash\n   # Test that you can switch back to v1.9.0\n   terraform version  # Should show v1.10.0\n\n   # Switch to v1.9.0\n   # Rerun plan - should work without breaking changes\n   ```\n\n2. **State file compatibility**:\n   - State files from v1.10.0 can be read by v1.9.0\n   - No state migration is needed\n   - Rolling back to v1.9.0 doesn't require special steps\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\nIf you encounter issues after upgrading to v1.10.0, you can safely rollback to v1.9.0:\n\n### Rollback Procedure\n\n1. **Switch back to Terraform v1.9.0**:\n   ```bash\n   # Using tfenv\n   tfenv install 1.9.0\n   tfenv use 1.9.0\n\n   # Or using direct binary\n   export PATH=\"/path/to/terraform-1.9.0:$PATH\"\n\n   # Verify\n   terraform version\n   ```\n\n2. **Revert configuration changes** (if you made them):\n   - Revert S3 backend to old attribute format if you changed it\n   - Revert moved block prefixes if you added resource.\n   - Continue using v1.9.0 code\n\n3. **No state file migration needed**:\n   ```bash\n   # State files are fully compatible between versions\n   terraform plan  # Should work immediately\n   ```\n\n4. **Identify the issue** that required rollback:\n   - Check if it's related to your custom configuration\n   - Review error messages for hints\n   - Search Terraform issues: https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues\n\n### Common Rollback Scenarios\n\n**Scenario: S3 backend assume_role block not working**\n```bash\n# Rollback and use the old deprecated attributes temporarily\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket     = \"my-bucket\"\n    key        = \"state\"\n    region     = \"us-east-1\"\n    role_arn   = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"  # Use old format\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**Scenario: Sensitive mark propagation breaking output validation**\n```bash\n# Rollback to v1.9.0\nterraform version\n# Check if the issue was specific to v1.10.0 behavior\n# If so, report the issue: https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/new\n```\n\n**Scenario: Ephemeral variables causing issues**\n```bash\n# Remove ephemeral = true from variables and outputs\n# Switch back to regular sensitive = true\nterraform {\n  # Clear any ephemeral configuration\n}\n```\n\n### When to Stay on v1.9.0\n\nConsider staying on v1.9.0 if:\n\n- You have critical workloads that cannot tolerate mark propagation changes\n- Your providers don't support ephemeral resources (not needed yet)\n- You need more time to update S3 backend configuration\n- You're waiting for certain ephemeral features (like module variables)\n\n### Migration Strategy\n\nFor safer upgrades:\n\n1. **Stage the upgrade**:\n   - Upgrade non-production workspaces first\n   - Test for 1-2 weeks\n   - Gradually upgrade production workspaces\n\n2. **Run both versions in parallel**:\n   - Keep v1.9.0 in one workspace\n   - Use v1.10.0 in another\n   - Compare results and behavior\n\n3. **Automated testing**:\n   - Add tests for sensitive mark behavior\n   - Test conditional expressions with sensitive values\n   - Validate S3 backend configuration\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Changes\n\n| Change | Impact | Action Required |\n|--------|--------|-----------------|\n| S3 backend deprecated attributes | Breaking | Migrate to `assume_role` block |\n| S3 backend new locking | Optional | Add `use_lockfile = true` if desired |\n| Moved block keyword prefixes | Breaking (rare) | Add `resource.` prefix if using reserved keywords |\n| Sensitive mark propagation | Behavioral | Review output redaction; use `nonsensitive()` if needed |\n| Ephemeral resources | New feature | Adopt for secret handling if desired |\n| Ephemeral variables | New feature | Mark sensitive variables as ephemeral |\n| Ephemeral outputs | New feature | Mark temporary outputs as ephemeral |\n\n---\n\n## Additional Resources\n\n- **Terraform v1.10.0 Release Notes**: https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/releases/tag/v1.10.0\n- **Terraform S3 Backend Documentation**: https://www.terraform.io/language/settings/backends/s3\n- **Terraform Moved Block Documentation**: https://www.terraform.io/language/state/moved\n- **Terraform Sensitive Values**: https://www.terraform.io/language/functions/sensitive\n- **Issue Tracker**: https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues\n\n---\n\n## Getting Help\n\nIf you encounter migration issues:\n\n1. **Check the error message** - it usually indicates the specific problem\n2. **Search existing issues** - your issue may already be reported\n3. **Open a new issue** with:\n   - Your Terraform configuration (with sensitive values redacted)\n   - The exact error message\n   - Steps to reproduce\n   - Your version information (`terraform version`)\n\n4. **Community resources**:\n   - Terraform Discuss: https://discuss.hashicorp.com/c/terraform-core/\n   - Stack Overflow: https://stackoverflow.com/questions/tagged/terraform\n\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

The most impactful changes involve:\n\n1. **S3 Backend Configuration** - Removal of deprecated IAM role attributes and migration to `assume_role` block syntax\n2. **Moved Blocks Syntax** - New requirement to prepend `resource.` when referencing resources with type names matching reserved keywords\n3. **Sensitive Value Handling** - Improved mark propagation in conditional expressions that may result in more values being marked as sensitive\n4. **Ephemeral Resources and Values** - New feature introducing ephemeral input variables, outputs, and resources that don't persist to state files\n\nThis guide walks you through each breaking change with detailed migration instructions and examples.\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. S3 Backend: Removal of Deprecated IAM Role Attributes\n\n#### What Changed\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 removes deprecated IAM role assumption attributes from the S3 backend configuration. These attributes have been replaced with the `assume_role` block syntax. The deprecated attributes are:\n\n- `role_arn`\n- `session_name`\n- `external_id`\n- `assume_role_duration_seconds`\n- `assume_role_policy`\n- `assume_role_policy_arns`\n- `assume_role_tags`\n- `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys`\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nThe `assume_role` block provides a cleaner, more structured configuration format that aligns with AWS SDK standards and is easier to maintain.
